# MGIA Grant Program
In accordance with the  [Montana Geospatial Information Act](http://leg.mt.gov/bills/mca/title_0900/chapter_0010/part_0040/sections_index.html) (MGIA), the Montana State Library administers a grant program to distribute accumulated funds from the Montana Geospatial Information Account, established by MGIA. Grant applications are evaluated by the State Library and its advisory council, the [Montana Geospatial Information Advisory Council,](https://msl.mt.gov/about/commission_councils/montana_land_information_advisory_council/index) and follow the  [MGIA Council Code of Ethics](http://docs.msl.mt.gov/aboutweb/documents/Code_of_Ethics_Adopted_1-28-10.pdf).  
  
The MGIA Grant Program supports state, local, tribal, and state university projects that advance the [Montana Geospatial Information Plan](https://docs.msl.mt.gov/MGIA/GeospatialPlans/FY26_28MontanaGeospatialInformationPlan.pdf) and improve the [Montana Spatial Data Infrastructure (MSDI)](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/data/msdi/) and other priority geospatial data and services. 
**FY2027 MGIA Grant Application Period Now Closed**
  * View Submitted Grants for the FY2027 MGIA Grant Program: [Link](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/Submitted_Applications)
  * MGIA Council will take action on prioritization of grant funding on [April 23, 2026](https://mslservices.mt.gov/ASPeN/Events/Event_Detail.aspx?Event_ID=31196)
  * MSL Commission will finalize grant funding on [May 6, 2026](https://mslservices.mt.gov/ASPeN/Events/Event_Detail.aspx?Event_ID=31769)
  * Please direct all questions to MGIAGrants@mt.gov
  * Grant Application Procedures & Instruction Forms: **[Download Zip](https://docs.msl.mt.gov/MGIA/grants/FY2027/MGIA_GrantApplication_FY2027.zip)**
  * FY2027 MGIA Grant Information Package: **[View/Download Package](https://docs.msl.mt.gov/MGIA/grants/FY2027/MGIAGrantProgramInfoPackage_FY2027.pdf)**


**Awarded Grant Projects:**
  * View Awarded Grant Projects: [_Link_  
](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/Awarded_MLIA_Grants)
  * MGIA Grant Projects History Dashboard (FY20-24): _[Link](https://arcg.is/11bfP)_

### **MGIA Grant Cycle Changes:**
There are notable changes in the grant program beginning with this cycle. MGIA Grants will now be awarded every two years, with a two year period of performance for funded projects.![image that describes the next 4 years of the grant program](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/GIS_Community/GIS_Coordination/MGIAGrantChangesImage.jpg)

# Natural Resource and Water Applications
[**Today's Air**](https://gis.mtdeq.us/portal/apps/experiencebuilder/experience/?id=000f42b119c44c7f9c3b4336470c721e)  
View current and historic air quality data at Montana's air quality monitoring stations.  
  
**[Department of Environmental Quality’s Online Query Service](https://discover-mtdeq.hub.arcgis.com/#SearchData)**  
Search several DEQ databases for information on facilities which may generate or handle hazardous wastes and sites that may contain potentially hazardous substances and/or petroleum products.
**[Mapping DEQ's Data](https://discover-mtdeq.hub.arcgis.com/)**  
View map locations of facilities, monitoring sites, and permits from several DEQ databases.
**[Montana Water Rights Query System](http://wrqs.dnrc.mt.gov/default.aspx)**  
Query, report, and map Montana's Department of Natural Resources and Conservation water right data.  
  
**[Montana Source Water Protection Program Query](https://deq.mt.gov/water/resources#/app/swp)**  
Search the Montana Department of Environmental Quality's Source Water Protection Program database for Source Water Assessments. Maps of Montana's public water supply assessment locations are available on the [Mapping DEQ's Data](https://discover-mtdeq.hub.arcgis.com/#SearchData) site.
**[](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/webmap/viewer.html?webmap=f59d958f8ec94e70b5a0bff9bb7dacae&extent=-116.1,44.5,-104.0,49.0)[Low Flow Data and Model Discovery Table](https://wa.water.usgs.gov/apps/LowFlowDataDiscoveryTable/)**  
Access information on low-flow and no-flow conditions in Montana streams. Developed by the USGS through a series of workshops with Federal, State, and Tribal partners, this comprehensive table simplifies the search for streamflow data. [Learn more](https://www.usgs.gov/tools/low-flow-data-and-model-discovery-table).
**[Channel Migration Zones](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/webmap/viewer.html?webmap=f59d958f8ec94e70b5a0bff9bb7dacae&extent=-116.1,44.5,-104.0,49.0)**  
View channel migration zone data for various rivers across Montana in an interactive web map environment
[**Relative Elevation Models**](https://storymaps.arcgis.com/stories/19b6bfe0c3aa454c853bd6d9b7228adf)  
Explore active and dry channels and fluvial features using LiDAR-derived relative elevation models
**[Groundwater Information Center (GWIC)](https://mbmg.mtech.edu/mapper/mapper.asp)**  
View ground water well locations and information in a Montana Bureau of Mines and Geology interactive web map environment.  
  
**[Clean Water Act Information Center (CWAIC) – Map Search](https://clean-water-act-information-center-mtdeq.hub.arcgis.com/)**  
Obtain information on federal and state mandated 305(b)/303(d) water quality reports, public comment, water quality laws, and Montana's water quality programs from the Department of Environmental Quality's public access clearinghouse.  
  
**[Montana Fisheries Information System](https://myfwp.mt.gov/fishMT/reports/surveyreport)**  
Investigate detailed fisheries and stream information on over 4,500 streams and lakes.  
  
**[NOAA National Climate Data Center](https://www.ncei.noaa.gov/maps-and-geospatial-products#app=cdo)**  
Browse climate and historical weather data.  
  
**[NRCS National Water and Climate](https://www.nrcs.usda.gov/programs-initiatives/sswsf-snow-survey-and-water-supply-forecasting-program/national-water-and)**  
Climate Monitoring Sites, Data, and Reports (snow, precipitation, soil moisture, reservoir storage, streamflow).  
  
**[MesoWest Surface Weather Maps](https://mesowest.utah.edu/cgi-bin/droman/mesomap.cgi?state=MT&rawsflag=3)**  
Access current and archived weather observations across Montana (and the United States).
**[2022 Montana Floods GIS Data Hub](https://montana-state-library-2022-floods-gis-data-hub-montana.hub.arcgis.com/)**  
Provides Montana Spatial Data Infrastructure (MSDI) and other GIS data for the 2022 Flood Disaster Declaration Counties.
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)

# Subject Guides
**[Montana Field Guide](http://fieldguide.mt.gov/)**  
Find information on identification, habitat, ecology, reproduction, range, and distribution of Montana's animals and plants, including species of concern, along with references and photographs.  
  
**[Montana Place Names Companion](https://www.mtmemory.org/pages/placenames)**  
Explore the location and origins of Montana's place names via this map, which is the companion to the book Montana Place Names from Alzada to Zortman written and published by the Montana Historical Society. Each point in the map links to an information item in the Montana History Portal collection [Montana Place Names from Alzada to Zortman](https://www.mtmemory.org/nodes/view/126018). This new site replaces the original application http://mtplacenames.org  
  
**[Montana Hunt Planner](https://fwp.mt.gov/gis/maps/huntPlanner/)**  
Find information about hunting in Montana.  
  
**[Montana Fishing Planner](https://myfwp.mt.gov/fishMT/explore)**  
Find information about fishing in Montana.  
  
**[Montana Activity Planner](https://fwp.mt.gov/activities)**  
Find the information that every recreationist needs for a successful Montana outdoor experience.
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)

# Tools
**[Web Map Services](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/data/web_services)**  
Access a select group of current GIS datasets via a live internet connection without downloading the data.  
  
**[Address Geocoder](https://ftpgeoinfo.msl.mt.gov/Documents/Applications/UsingMSLGeocodingService.pdf)**  
Convert street addresses into geographic coordinates (i.e. Latitude/Longitude).  
  
**[Montana State Plane Coordinate Conversion](http://nris.mt.gov/gis/projection/)**  
Convert back and forth between Latitude/Longitude coordinates and Montana State Plane Coordinates.
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)

### Public & Tribal College Libraries Snapshot
![](https://msl.mt.gov/about/publications/statistics/Session2025-Infographic-Horizontal.png)  

  * Montanans access information through 82 public libraries, 30 public library branches, and 7 tribal college libraries. Communities surrounding Billings, Bozeman, Great Falls, Helena, and Livingston also receive service from 6 bookmobiles.
  * Montanans visited their public and tribal college libraries an average of 3 times throughout the year, for a total of 3,265,611 visits in fiscal year 2024.
  * Montana library patrons checked out 5.5 million items in 2024, over 5 items per capita. 31% of those checkouts were done via a mobile device from electronic collections such as MontanaLibrary2Go using the Libby app. Electronic collections curated by Montana librarians give readers access anytime and anywhere to the information they need.
  * Through the State Library's Hotspot Lending Program, patrons in 51 counties borrowed hotspots from 88 libraries to access the Internet. Together, these patrons used over 950 Terabytes of data in FY 2024 to complete homework, search for employment, apply for jobs, and keep informed of current events. Hotspots also helped reduce social isolation with 45% of users reporting they used the devices to connect with family and friends.
  * The Montana Courier Alliance facilitated the movement of 421,391 books between libraries in FY 2024 (a 41% increase from FY 2019), exemplifying the efforts of public libraries to maximize value for their communities. This service allows patrons, such as a reader in Terry, to request a book from Ennis, which is then delivered alongside other requested materials in an efficient, cost-effective manner. By reducing redundant purchases and shipping expenses, the courier system enables local libraries to focus on curating collections that best meet the needs of their communities.

#### State Aid
[State aid handout (printable version of the below information)](https://msl.mt.gov/about/publications/about-the-library/2025_StateAid.pdf)
![](https://msl.mt.gov/about/publications/statistics/Session2025-Infographic_OperatingRev-Horizontal.png)
The 2023 Legislature reauthorized state aid to public libraries, increasing aid from $0.40 per capita to $0.50 per capita. At the same time, Legislature revised the definition of public libraries to include accredited tribal college libraries that provide services to the public.
According to Montana Public Library Standards which are established in Administrative Rule, a public library defined at 22-1-301(3), MCA, and created under Title 7, MCA, shall derive at least 70% of its revenue from local tax revenues (ARM 10.102.1158). This standard ensures that state aid supplements but does not supplant local tax support. In the last fiscal year, state aid made up 1% of total public library operating revenue with local revenue contributing 89% and the remaining 10% in grants, donations, and other similar one time resources. 
Example 1: Billings Public Library
  * State Aid: **$70,544** (1%)
  * Local Revenue: **$4,010,607** (81%)
  * Total Operating Revenue: **$4,925,759**


Example 2: Wibaux County Library
  * State Aid: **$805**(1%)
  * Local Revenue: **$122,734**(97%)
  * Total Operating Revenue: **$126,003  
**


(Public Libraries Survey, 2024)
Under the same Administrative Rule, a tribal college library that serves the public is required to receive recognition and support from the tribal council in its work to obtain funding (ARM 10.102.1158). This effort is mainly in the form of seeking federal grants. Four tribal college libraries met the standards to receive state aid in FY 2024 and received payment this fall:
  * Aaniiih Nakoda College Library - **$2,232.50**
  * James E. Shanley Tribal Library - **$3,558.00**
  * Stone Child College Library - **$2,046.00**
  * Woodenlegs Library - **$2,315.50**


Because payment was first received in FY 2025, the example below reflects operating revenue pre-state aid.
Example: Woodenlegs Library
  * Federal Revenue: **$95,360**(100%)
  * Other Revenue: **$0**(0%)
  * Total Operating Revenue: **$95,360**


(Public Libraries Survey, 2024)

  4. In-Person Reference Services


# Digital First Reference Services
Montana State Library is a special government library in which items from our collection are either mailed to patrons or fully accessible online. We follow a digital first reference service model with in-person references services available by appointment.
Montana State Library offers in-person reference services by appointment. To make an appointment, please email: MSLAppointment@mt.gov or call: (406) 444-3115. If you know the staff member you would like to meet, you can contact them directly. Phone numbers and emails for each staff member can be found at our [Staff Directory](https://mslservices.mt.gov/About_the_Library/about_Staff).
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)
#### CONTACT US:
  * **PO Box 201800, or  
1201 11th Ave   
Helena, Montana 59620 **
  * Hours: Monday-Friday   
8AM-5PM


  * Phone: (406) 444-3115   
Toll Free: (800) 338-5087   
TTY: Montana Relay 711

![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSshort_4cp1.jpg)
##  **The Story of the Montana State Library Logo**
* * *
### **Visually reflecting our value to Montanans**
Our logo represents the full spectrum of what we do. Like the prism that refracts a beam of light into brilliance, the Montana State Library collects and synthesizes information of all kind to impart a greater state of knowledge to our users.
![MSL Logo Description](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL_LogoAnatomy-Top-Half.png)
**Knowledge about Montana,**  
**for Montanans, by Montanans.**
![MSL Logo Color Palette](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL_LogoAnatomy-Bottom-Half.png)
* * *
#### **More than just a new logo**
Our refreshed brand is founded on these five tenets which unite our efforts, communicate our value, and bring visibility to our mission: 
#### **ACCESS**
Our open-data advocacy helps equalize the knowledge base of Montanans.
#### **TRUST**
We are non-partisan with a reputation for integrity and transparency that fosters strong relationships across the state.
#### **PURPOSE**
All areas of the State Library contribute to making lives better for Montanans.
#### **EFFICIENCY**
We promote data-sharing that expedites decisions and leads to better outcomes.
#### **LEADING EDGE**
We anticipate the information needs of Montanans which results in innovative product and service offerings.
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)

# Welcome
![](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL_ColorBars.jpg)
![Jennie Stapp](http://docs.msl.mt.gov/aboutweb/images/JennieStapp.jpg) **Jennie Stapp**   
**Montana****State Librarian**
The Montana State Library is committed to strengthening libraries and information services for all Montanans through leadership, advocacy, and service. The outstanding staff and partners of the State Library strive to meet this mission every day.
International library strategist Lorcan Dempsey challenges librarians to think about how we can collaborate to solve infrastructure challenges in ways that improve economies of scale, which then permit librarians and information professionals to focus more resources on innovation and opportunities for community engagement.
Through consulting services, education, and creative collaboration, we at the State Library focus much of our energy and creative resources to support the infrastructure on which our partners rely. And we challenge ourselves and our partners to be innovative collaborators in our communities. As a result, Montana libraries are better positioned to be their communities’ choice for discovery and exchange of information and ideas. Our dedication to strengthening libraries and information services for all strengthens community life for all Montanans.
I speak for all Montana information professionals when I say that we look forward to helping you with your information needs, either in person or online. Welcome to the Montana State Library!
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)
#### CONTACT US:
  * **PO Box 201800, or  
1201 11th Ave   
Helena, Montana 59620 **

8AM-5PM


  * Phone: (406) 444-3115   
Toll Free: (800) 338-5087

## Using Our Services
### Digital First Reference Services
![](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/Digital-Search-MSL.png)
Montana State Library is a special government library in which items from our collection are either mailed to patrons or fully accessible online. We follow a digital first reference service model with in-person references services available by appointment.
To make an appointment, please email: MSLAppointment@mt.gov or call: (406) 444-3115. If you know the staff member you would like to meet, you can contact them directly. Phone numbers and emails for each staff member can be found at our [Staff Directory](https://mslservices.mt.gov/About_the_Library/about_Staff).
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)
#### CONTACT US:
  * **PO Box 201800, or  
1201 11th Ave   
Helena, Montana 59620 **
  * Hours: Monday-Friday   
8AM-5PM


  * Phone: (406) 444-3115   
Toll Free: (800) 338-5087   
TTY: Montana Relay 711
  * [Accessibility Statement](https://msl.mt.gov/accessibility)

# Accessibility Statement
The Montana State Library strives to meet accessibility guidelines as described in the World Wide Web Consortium's [Web Content Accessibility Guidelines v2.1](https://www.w3.org/TR/WCAG21/) conformance level AA.
Contact Kenny Ketner, Information Products Lead, to resolve any accessibility issues with the MSL website. MSL will provide effective communication of any information you are unable to access due to a barrier upon receipt of your email.
## Accessibility Plug-ins and Viewers
  * Adobe Acrobat  
Use [Adobe Acrobat](https://get.adobe.com/reader/) to read Portable Document Format (PDF) files.
  * Microsoft Word  
Microsoft offers [Doc Viewer](https://apps.microsoft.com/detail/9n69kfjds28z) and other converter programs to enable those who do not have Word to open and view Word files.
  * Microsoft Excel  
Microsoft offers [XLS Viewer Free](https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/p/xls-viewer-free/9nblggh6hbf5) to enable those who do not have Excel to view Excel files.
  * Microsoft PowerPoint  
Microsoft offers [PPTX Viewer](https://apps.microsoft.com/detail/9np64t9094lb) to enable those who do not have PowerPoint to view PowerPoint files.


## Accessibility Feedback Form
This form is intended for users to share feedback about any accessibility barriers or challenges encountered while using our websites, applications, or digital services. The information you provide will help our team identify, investigate, and address accessibility issues so we can improve access for all users. Details submitted through this form may be shared with relevant staff and contractors solely for the purpose of troubleshooting and remediation. This form is not an official channel for filing ADA or Section 508 complaints, and it should not be used to report emergencies or time‑sensitive issues; for formal complaints or urgent assistance, please use the contact options listed on our main accessibility or contact page.
## Contact Information
Name*
Name*
First Name
Last Name
Would you like a response about this issue?*
Would you like a response about this issue? Required field
Yes
No
After you submit this form, your feedback will be reviewed by our accessibility team and routed to the appropriate staff for follow‑up and remediation planning. In most cases, we aim to acknowledge your submission within 5 days and, if you requested a response, provide an update or request additional details within 30 days. Actual resolution timelines may vary depending on the complexity of the issue and the systems involved. Please note that we may not be able to provide individual status updates for every report, but all feedback is logged and used to improve the accessibility of our websites, applications, and digital services.
Preferred Contact Method

Phone
Email Address
Email address will only be used to follow up on the issue if selected above.

  4. Web Map Services


# Web Map Services
Web map services allow your applications to connect to and use on-line GIS datasets. The State Library offers the services listed below. Anyone may view the services in their web browser by clicking on the service names below and then choosing the _ArcGIS Online Map Viewer_ link near the top of the service's home page.
  * **30-day Notice for Web Service Change Policy:** The Montana State Library has formalized a life cycle support [policy for MSL web services](https://docs.msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/governance/Life-Cycle-Support-Policy-MSL-Web-Services-30-day-Notice.pdf?utm_medium=email&utm_source=govdelivery). 
    * Routine maintenance (data edits, adding fields) will not require advance notice, though we will notify you of planned disruptions expected to be longer than 2 hours.
    * Removal of services and substantive changes — such as removing feature classes, tables, or fields, or renaming/relocating a service — will require 30 day advance notice. Reminders will follow weekly for the two weeks prior to the change, and again the day before.
    * When a service undergoes a substantive change, a new version will be published alongside the previous version for the full 30-day period before the old version is retired.
    * All notices will be distributed through MSL's GovDelivery. [Subscribe to GovDelivery](https://public.govdelivery.com/accounts/MTLIBRARY/subscriber/new)


  * **Note** : The presence of a map service, the data schema, and the data itself are subject to change as resources allow and the data or the service improves and is updated. To stay informed about changes to these web map services, join the [MAGIP listserv](http://www.magip.org/ListServe) or subscribe to the [MSL news feed](https://public.govdelivery.com/accounts/MTLIBRARY/subscriber/new?topic_id=MTLIBRARY_17). Direct questions about a specific web map service to the respective [MSDI Theme Steward](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/data/msdi/index).
  * **ArcGIS Desktop Users** may use this URL -- https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/ -- in the "Add ArcGIS server" dialog box to access the main list of services. You may also use the _View In ArcMap_ link on the service home pages listed below to add the services to your map documents. See the [ArcGIS Help](https://desktop.arcgis.com/en/arcmap/latest/map/working-with-arcmap/connect-to-arcgis-server-from-arcgis-desktop.htm##//01540000047m000000) for assistance with connecting to services from ArcMap. Or, [ArcGIS Pro](https://pro.arcgis.com/en/pro-app/latest/help/projects/connect-to-a-gis-server.htm) Help for assistance connecting to services in ArcGIS Pro.
  * **Web Mercator projection** : Unless otherwise noted these services use the Web Mercator coordinate system, which facilitates their incorporation into web map applications. _Users of ArcMap must make sure that the coordinate systems of their data frames are never set to Web Mercator_ if they want to perform any kind of measurements. Most web applications understand that the map scale varies as you move north and south in this coordinate system, but ArcMap mostly does not. Measurements made in Montana will be from 40 percent to 100 percent too large if they are made using the Web Mercator projection.


#### Montana Spatial Data Infrastructure Services
  * **[Boundaries](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/Boundaries/MapServer)** : This contains the layers of the [Montana Administrative Boundaries Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/administrative_boundaries/index), which includes the State boundary, counties, school districts, incorporated cities and towns, Tribal Nations Reservations, weed management districts, tax increment financing districts, and Election Districts including voting precincts and county commissioner districts. 
  * **[Cadastral](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/Parcels/MapServer)** : This shows the [Montana Cadastral Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/cadastral/index), with the boundaries of Montana's tax parcels. 
    * [**Public Land Survey**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/PLSS/MapServer): This shows the [Montana Public Land Survey System](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/cadastral/CadNSDI) of townships, ranges, sections, and section subdivisions.
    * [**Public Lands**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/PublicLands/MapServer): This shows [Public Lands](https://mslservices.mt.gov/Geographic_Information/Data/DataList/datalist_Details.aspx?did={60b5a8b0-b272-11e2-9e96-0800200c9a66}) that are recorded in the Montana Department of Revenue's tax appraisal database. 
    * [**Conservation Easements**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/ConservationEasements/MapServer): This show private lands parcels on which a public agency or qualified Land Trust has placed a [Conservation Easement](https://mslservices.mt.gov/Geographic_Information/Data/DataList/datalist_Details.aspx?did={9d69b262-b766-11e2-bc7e-f23c91aec05e}) in cooperation with the land owner. 
  * [**Geographic Names**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/GeoNames/MapServer): This contains the [Montana Geographic Names Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/geographic_names/index).
  * [**Hydrography**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/Hydrography/MapServer): This shows the lakes, streams, and other water features of the [Montana Hydrography Dataset](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/hydrography/index).
  * **[Land Cover](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/Montana_Land_Cover/MapServer):** This shows the [Montana Land Use/Land Cover Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/land_use_land_cover/index).
  * **[Managed Areas:](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/ManagedAreas/MapServer)** This shows public and private [Managed Areas](https://mslservices.mt.gov/Geographic_Information/Data/DataList/datalist_Details.aspx?did={80C2319F-17BC-4A67-B0DF-BB12B53D1D5E}) and information on special land designations.
  * **[Mapping Control:](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/MappingControl/MapServer)** This show the [Mapping Control Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/mapping_control) submitted by registered land surveyors or GIS professionals
  * **Orthoimagery (Air Photo) Services** showing the National Agricultural Imagery Program (NAIP) photos for [**2023**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2023/ImageServer), [**2021**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2021/ImageServer), **[2019](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2019/ImageServer)** , **[2017](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2017/ImageServer)** , **[2015](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2015/ImageServer)** ,**[2013](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2013/ImageServer)** , **[2011](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2011/ImageServer)** , **[2009](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2009/ImageServer)** , and **[2005](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2005/ImageServer)** are available. The 2009-2019 services may be displayed as color infrared images by choosing to show bands 4, 1, and 2 as the red, green and blue bands. The 2005 service is only natural-color, but a separate service is available for infrared images taken in **[2005 and 2006](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/NAIP_2005CIR/ImageServer)**.
  * [**Soils**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/Soils/MapServer): This shows the [Soils (SSURGO) framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/soils/index).
  * [**Structures and Addresses**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/MontanaStructuresAddresses/MapServer): This shows the [Montana Structures and Addresses Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/structures_and_addresses/index).
  * [**Transportation**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/MontanaTransportation/MapServer): This shows the road centerlines from the [Montana Transportation Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/transportation/index).
  * **[Watershed Boundaries](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/WatershedBoundaries/MapServer)** : This shows the [Hydrologic Units Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/hydrologic_units/index).
  * [**Wetlands/Riparian**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/WetlandsRiparian/MapServer): This shows the [Montana Wetlands and Riparian Areas Framework](https://msl.mt.gov/geoinfo/msdi/wetlands/index).


#### Other Services
  * **[Montana Address Locator](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/MontanaAddressLocator/GeocodeServer)** : This service converts street addresses into geographic coordinates (i.e. Latitude/Longitude).
  * [**Geographic Names Locator**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSDI_Framework/GeographicsNamesLocator/GeocodeServer): This service converts geographic names into coordinates.
  * [**State Mask:**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/StateMask/MapServer) This service may be used for covering map data that is not in selected states or provinces of North America or counties near Montana.
  * [**State Base Map**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/StateBaseMap/MapServer): This service may be used as a general base map and has a map data overlay group for imagery services. The emphasis is on public and private land ownership data. It also shows the Public Land Survey System, lakes and streams, roads, and landforms.
  * **[Digital Orthophoto Quarter Quadrangle Data (DOQQ)](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/DOQQ_1990s/ImageServer)** : This is a mosaic of black and white orthorectified aerial photos of Montana and Yellowstone National Park taken predominantly in the 1990s. The mosaic footprint layer has an attribute field called Image_Year that gives the year the image was taken and a field called Image_Main_Date that gives the first date from the USGS metadata for the image.
  * [**Historic Imagery (Mid 20th Century)**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/Historic_Imagery_Mid20thCentury/ImageServer): This image service is a mosaic of black and white historical aerial images from the USGS Single Frame Archive creating a continuous orthoimage for Montana. The imagery spans the 1940s to the 1970s. A web service of the [Image Dates](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/item.html?id=48101174174243aaaaba3d55920b9312) and [Tile Index](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/item.html?id=f2136a350af148d0acc38b3b0c13c2f6) are also available for reference. 
  * **[Historic Topographic Maps](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/HistoricTopo/MapServer)** : These 1:24,000 and 1:100,000 scale topographic maps were the newest scanned maps available from the U.S. Geological Survey TopoView web site as of November 2015. The data include the maps covering Montana and parts of Idaho and northern Wyoming. The data provides a historical reference and because they contain hand-placed elevation and place names the information may not be available on newer maps. Users should be aware that significant changes may have occurred in the landscape since the maps were made as many of the maps are over 30 years old.
  * [**Frost Free Days**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/FrostFreeDays/ImageServer): This raster data can be used as a tool to determine growing season and suitability for certain crops. The data represent the spatial distribution of the number of days in which the daily minimum temperature is greater than 32 degrees Fahrenheit based on a 5 in 10 year probability.
  * [**Relative Effective Annual Precipitation (REAP)**](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/RelativeEffectiveAnnualPrecipitation/ImageServer): The Montana REAP data represents a 30-year precipitation data period sensitized to the landscape according to slope and aspect, then calibrated by soil scientists to known vegetation breaks on the landscape based on imagery, field experience, and published SSURGO/NASIS soils data.
  * **[Flathead Basin 2009 Orthophotos and Elevation](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/item.html?id=4e470ca90a4c42af96f4a2b34c7e0045)** : This shows high-resolution air photos, [infrared air photos](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/item.html?id=9e7757760c6f4b8d8695a421a769dfb9), [contours](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/item.html?id=4028882bb13f445aa97374c6eaeda17f), and [digital elevation model](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/item.html?id=ee0a762b06b74422a3067e29473d9b23) collected for the northern Flathead valley and the shorelines of Flathead Lake in 2009. A [**web map**](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/webmap/viewer.html?webmap=fcb84f3ec8b04215824e854ea7c6f33f) and **[web app](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/item.html?id=5b6c1f60bc124c4189257fe2cdefb742)** of this service is available for easier access to the data for users not using GIS software.
  * [**Yellowstone River Hydrology**](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/home/item.html?id=e04b577551664fb38759fd042f46c551): This service shows data collected for the Yellowstone River Cumulative Effects Analysis, including the channel migration zone, historic locations of the river channel, man-made features that impact the flow of the river, river reaches, and river miles. A [**web map**](https://montana.maps.arcgis.com/apps/webappviewer/index.html?id=3fc5b219f4494ebab2477e93a5bbecca) of this service is available for easier access to the data for users not using GIS software.
  * **[Reference100k](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/Reference100k/ImageServer)** : This service provides a static base map of Montana designed to be viewed at a scale of approximately 1:100,000. Data shown on the map includes public land ownership, selected federal and state managed areas, lakes, streams, roads, the Public Land Survey system, 50-foot contours, shaded relief, and selected buildings and structures. A [cached version](https://gisservicemt.gov/arcgis/rest/services/MSL/Reference100k_cached/ImageServer) is also available.

## Montana Library Network
> ### A collaborative community of Montana libraries working together to provide all Montanans with library content and services sufficient unto their needs.
### Montana Library Network (MLN)
[ Key Principles ](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/Montana-Library-Network#accordion1-collapse1)
**_Key Principles_**
Our success is measured by our users’ successes. 
Collaboration makes our services efficient. 
Local librarians know best the needs of their communities, and how to meet these needs.
Montana libraries decide how or if they participate in MLN. 
We learn from others. 
We are future focused.
We work to improve what we do and how we do it, focusing on the present and future needs of our communities.
We explore, try, test, pilot, and adapt to new and changing programs and services. 
[ Montana Library Network News ](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/Montana-Library-Network#accordion1-collapse2)

# Contact Us
The Montana State Library provides continuing education, consulting, programming, and consortial services to libraries across Montana. 
  

### [Library Development](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/library_development/index)

# About the Public Libraries Survey
The Montana Public Libraries Survey (PLS), also referred to as the Public Library Annual Statistical Report, provides statistics on the status of public libraries in Montana. It is also required under [Administrative Rule 10.102.1155](https://rules.mt.gov/gateway/RuleNo.asp?RN=10%2E102%2E1155 "https://rules.mt.gov/gateway/ruleno.asp?rn=10%2e102%2e1155") and the [Public Library Standards](https://rules.mt.gov/gateway/ruleno.asp?RN=10.102.1158 "https://rules.mt.gov/gateway/ruleno.asp?rn=10.102.1158") to receive State Aid. These statistics are in turn submitted to the [Institute of Museum and Library Services (IMLS)](https://www.imls.gov/research-evaluation/surveys/public-libraries-survey-pls), allowing peer comparisons between libraries of similar variables across the country. 
Data includes information about library visits, circulation, size of collections, public service hours, staffing, electronic resources, operating revenues and expenditures and number of service outlets. These data are used by federal, state and local officials, professional associations, and local practitioners for planning, evaluation, and policy making.
##### [ Complete the Survey  Submit your survey using Counting Opinions LibPAS (opens October 1)  ](https://mt.countingopinions.com)
##### [ Dashboards & Resources  Access PLS data and reports. Review survey collection status.  ](https://msl.mt.gov/about/publications/publiclibrarystatistics)
##### [ Video Tutorials  YouTube play list of recorded tutorials regarding the PLS  ](https://youtube.com/playlist?list=PLRaydtZpHu2qDY-vKYe5-qJt_jGTL3yZD&feature=shared)
##### [ Knowledge Base  Visit MSL's Library Research & Evaluation knowledge base (more articles coming soon)  ](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/sp?id=kb_view2&kb_id=597c9d7687200e503f5e0e56cebb3513)
##### [ Support Desk  Request support from the Public Libraries Survey or Library Research & Evaluation team  ](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/citizen?id=sc_cat_item&sys_id=872155fd87080614d49cc9d5cebb3549)
##### [ Definitions  Excel workbook with the data element definitions including question source (federal or state) and entry specifications  ](https://msl.mt.gov/about/publications/statistics/PLS_Definitions_2025.xlsx)
##### [ Survey Worksheet  PDF worksheet to help directors prepare their responses for entry into Counting Opinions  ](https://msl.mt.gov/about/publications/statistics/PLS_Worksheet_2025.pdf)
##### [ Staff Workbook  Excel workbook to collect the data needed for the Staff Information section of the survey  ](https://msl.mt.gov/about/publications/statistics/PLS_StaffingInformation_2025.xlsx)
##### [ Program Tracking Template  Excel template for tracking programs throughout the year  ](https://msl.mt.gov/about/publications/about-the-library/TEMPLATE_Program_Tracking.xlsx)

## Continuing Education
#### _Montana State Library is charged with_
  * Promoting the value of continuing education
  * Encouraging boards to support continuing education for library staff
  * Developing and providing quality training in all formats
  * Keeping Montana librarians informed of continuing education opportunities

# Library Services Support
MSL Library Services provides support for ASPeN, Montana History Portal, Montana Shared Catalog, Public Libraries Survey, and Statewide Projects.
### Support Requests
  

To submit a support request, you will need an Okta account, which you may already have to use various State resources. For instance, if you have an account to log in to ASPeN, you already have an Okta account.
  

  * Click the submit link below.
  * Log in to Okta.
  * Choose Citizen login unless you work for a State Agency.


[Submit a Library Services support request](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/citizen?id=sc_cat_item&sys_id=872155fd87080614d49cc9d5cebb3549)[](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/citizen?id=sc_cat_item&sys_id=872155fd87080614d49cc9d5cebb3549)
  

If you need to create an Okta account, please follow these instructions.
[Create an Okta account](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/citizen?sys_kb_id=17bd8a68876dca54915586e7cebb3550&id=kb_article_view&sysparm_rank=2&sysparm_tsqueryId=25390eb4873d069043200f28cebb35cd)
### Knowledge Bases
The knowledge bases in each of these service areas contain articles, instructions, and information.
##### [ ASPeN  Your source for continuing education, certification tracking, and directory information. ](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/sp?id=kb_view2&kb_id=4ecad1be87ecca503f5e0e56cebb3507)
##### [ Montana History Portal  An online source for digital collections relating to Montana's cultural heritage. ](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/sp?id=kb_view2&kb_id=5947153e87acca503f5e0e56cebb3500)
##### [ Montana Shared Catalog  A consortium of multi-type libraries serving communities across the state. ](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/sp?id=kb_view2&kb_id=0822c1be87e4ca503f5e0e56cebb3592)
##### [ Research & Evaluation  Library data, dashboards, and required reports such as the Public Libraries Survey, Federation Grants, and Standards. ](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/sp?id=kb_view2&kb_id=597c9d7687200e503f5e0e56cebb3513)
##### [ Statewide Projects  Statewide Projects includes MontanaLibrary2Go, Montana Courier Alliance, Hot Spot Lending Program, and OCLC. ](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/sp?id=kb_view2&kb_id=7d3e51be87200e503f5e0e56cebb350e)

# Federations
Montana is divided up into six regions. Libraries within those regions have formed a federation. It's a formal and informal way to network and improve library services in Montana.
![Map of Montana Library Federations](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/library_development/Trustees/fedmap.jpg)
### Consultants
##  Tracy Cook [](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/library_development/Federations#collapse-Tile1)
Lead Consulting and Learning Librarian
  * Golden Plains
  * Sagebrush


##  Cara Orban [](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/library_development/Federations#collapse-Tile2)
Statewide Consulting Librarian
  * South Central
  * Tamarack


##  Corey Sloan [](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/library_development/Federations#collapse-Tile3)
Statewide Consulting Librarian
  * Broad Valleys
  * Pathfinder

# Hot Spot Lending Program
### Hot Spot Program
[ Point of Contacts and Support ](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/hotspotlendingprogram#accordion1-collapse1)
  1. **_T-Mobile_**
     * [Portal Link: T-Mobile](https://statelocalgov.tmorders.com/portal/dashboard)
       * Portals allow you to suspend/unsuspend devices, order device replacements, name/rename devices, activate new devices/SIMS, review billing and make payments, create/download reports, etc.
     * _Ticket Support:_ tmsupport@inseego.com
     * _Advanced Support_ : Shankman@T-Mobile.com & Mark.Serrano66@T-Mobile.com
  2. **_Verizon_**
       * _[Portal Link: Verizon](https://mblogin.verizonwireless.com/account/business/login/unifiedlogin)_
         * Portals allow you to suspend/unsuspend devices, order device replacements, name/rename devices, activate new devices/SIMS, review billing and make payments, create/download reports, etc.
       * _Support Hotline:_wfmvzwbusinesssupport@vzw.com


  1. [**Montana State Library Ticket System**](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/library_services_support)
     * We are happy to help with directions or set up a video call, but we will not have access to portals to make changes.

[ Troubleshooting ](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/hotspotlendingprogram#accordion1-collapse4)
  1. **First Step- Make sure information matches! The information physically in your device (not on the box) needs to match what you have in the portal.**
    1. **SIM #** (The SIM card associated with your hotspot). This number is physically on the small chip inside your device.
    2. **IMEI #** (the hotspot’s unique identification number- # can be found underneath the battery) _Note- IMEI is less important for T-Mobile, but important for identifying device._
    3. **“Active” Status:** make sure the device in the portal is active and not suspended or been removed.
    4. **NOTE-** NEVER swap SIM cards! More devices will start having issues!


  1. **Factory Reset:**


A common solution to many connectivity and hotspot operational issues is to perform a Factory Reset. This will reset all of the device’s settings to the default values, including admin passwords, Wi-Fi name (SSID), and system settings.
  1. Within a hotspot you can find a “Factory Reset” button or tab.   
1. Remove the back cover and while the hotspot has charge.  
2. Hold down this button or tab. Sometimes a small tool like a paperclip is needed.  
3. Hold the button down for a few seconds until the screen starts rebooting.
  2. Alternatively, factory resets can also be done through the T-Mobile or Verizon admin screens on a computer  
  
[T-Mobile online factory reset instructions  
](https://www.t-mobile.com/support/tutorials/device/t-mobile/hotspot/topic/update-amp-backup/how-to-perform-a-factory-reset)[Verizon online factory reset instructions](https://www.verizon.com/support/knowledge-base-55839/)


3. **Put in a Support Ticket:**
**_T-Mobile:_**
  1. _Ticket Support:_tmsupport@inseego.com
  2. _Phone Support:_ 1-800-307-0340
  3. _Help Center:_<https://inseego.clickhelp.co/home/en-us/>
  4. _Advanced Support_ : Shankman@T-Mobile.com & Mark.Serrano66@T-Mobile.com


**_Verizon:_**
  1. _Ticket Support:_wfmvzwbusinesssupport@vzw.com
  2. _Phone Support:_ 1-800-525-0481
  3. _Help Center: Top of Screen > _Click Support > Get Support OR >Troubleshooting


[**Montana State Library Ticket System  
**](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/library_services_support)We are happy to help with directions or set up a video call, but we will not have access to portals to make changes.
[ Circulation Policies and Templates ](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/hotspotlendingprogram#accordion1-collapse5)
**_Example Circulation Policies/Templates for Hot Spot Programs_**
  * **[Arizona State Library User Agreement Template  
](https://azlibrary.gov/sites/default/files/libdev_wifi_progdesc_2020.pdf)**_9 and 10 of this PDF have a template user agreement that you could adapt for your library_
  * [**Butte Silver-Bow Hotspot Agreement**](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/HotSpot-agreement-BSBPL.pdf)


**_Suggested Check-In Procedure  
_**If a patron states, the device is no longer working, it may have been suspended by the hotspot manager for it being overdue. The front desk should send the hotspot to the hotspot manager, because they will need to unsuspend in the portal or do further troubleshooting.
Tampering Tape- This can help prevent SIM cards from being swapped/stolen. If tampering tape has been broken, front desk can send it to the “hotspot” manager to ensure everything is still working and correct in the portal.
**_Suggested Overdue Procedures for Hot Spots  
_**We suggest having a consistent day/time to check for overdue hotspots in your cataloging system, potentially once a week. After that time, you can:
Suspend the respective [T-Mobile](https://statelocalgov.tmorders.com/portal/dashboard) or [Verizon](https://www.verizon.com/business/login) hotspot using your library's hotspot management portal.
Suspending a hotspot will pause all data usage on the hotspot, often prompting the hotspot to be returned. When the device is returned, ensure its suspension is reverted. Once confirmed that the hotspot has active data usage, it can then go back into circulation.
 __NOTE__ : Suspending a device will pause charges to that device. Both T-Mobile and Verizon have a max suspension with no billing per year, but it can help with replacement costs if necessary. T-Mobile: $30 for 1 month; Verizon is $40 for one month. You can suspend a device for one more month, but after two consecutive months full billing will resume. It would be best to decide to replace the device or cancel the line at the 30 or 60 days of no return.
**_  
Fines and Fees with Hot Spots_**
For Montana Shared Catalog libraries, fine options are:  
No fines  
10 cents per day  
$1.00 per day
[ Cataloging & Record Keeping ](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/hotspotlendingprogram#accordion1-collapse6)
**_Hot Spot Device Tracking and Record-Keeping_**
**The most important pieces of information to keep track of are:**
  1. **Line #** (this takes the form of a traditional 10-digit phone number)
  2. **SIM #** (The SIM card associated with your hotspot). This number is physically on the card.
  3. **IMEI #** (the hotspot’s unique identification number- # can be found underneath the battery) _Note- IMEI is less important for T-Mobile, but important for identifying device._
  4. **Provider Name-** if you use more than one provider.


**_How to Catalog this Information:  
_**The information provided above can be put into **_“STAFF”_** notes when cataloging within Workflows.
Creating an organized Excel sheet with your device information is additionally recommended with the above information each being it’s own column- plus a notes section.
****** Be sure when you are cataloging your items that the IMEI Number directly underneath the battery correlates to the information in your cataloging system. ******
**Note** : For your cataloging needs you can decide on a naming convention that makes sense for your patrons and staff, but please ensure that your management records at least keep track of the above information.
_Naming Your Devices in the Portal & Cataloging:_
T-Mobile:
  * Click/Open the line number in the Portal
  * Find User Defined Info- Click Edit
  * Edit Section Called “Library” to be the same as what you have in your catalog system. 
    * You can use whatever naming convention that works best for your library: Hotspot 1, Hotspot #### (last 4 of your line number, etc.


Verizon:
  * Click/Open the line number in the Portal
  * Under “User Information” at the top- Click Edit
  * Edit First Name as Hotspot and/or Branch name, Edit Last Name as the number of your hotspot as you have it cataloged/named in your catalog system.

[ Billing Information ](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/hotspotlendingprogram#accordion1-collapse7)
Billing is automatically set up to be a **__monthly bill__** for both T-Mobile and Verizon.
**_T-Mobile Bill Period:_** 10th-9th. Billing is accessible in [Portal](https://statelocalgov.tmorders.com/portal/index/index).  
Billing Statement e-mailed between 13th-16th.
**_Verizon Bill Period:_** 6th-5th. Billing is accessible in [Portal](https://mb.verizonwireless.com/mbt/secure/index?appName=esm#/esm/dashboard).   
Billing Statement e-mailed within a week.
[**T-Mobile Manage Billing Settings Directions** :](https://www.t-mobile.com/support/business/account-hub-billing) Paper/Paperless- Email Notifications  
 _**Note- you will want to log-in with Government Portal for T-Mobile, but the directions are the same _except_ for the “Account Hub” link._
[**Verizon Manage Billing Settings Directions:**](https://www.verizon.com/business/support/billing-and-payments/my-business-wireless/manage-billing/) Paper/Paperless- Email Notifications
**_Specialty Billing:_** Providers can set up a special paying period/statement if you would prefer to bulk pay for multiple months.
_T-Mobile POC_ : Alexander.Shankman@T-Mobile.com
_Verizon POC_ : cynthia.romano@verizonwireless.com

**[Montana State Hot Spot Program FAQs](https://montana.servicenowservices.com/citizen?id=kb_category&kb_id=7d3e51be87200e503f5e0e56cebb350e&kb_category=405cd4288715461016eabae9cebb3582)**
[ Program Data July 2020 – June 2025 ](https://msl.mt.gov/libraries/hotspotlendingprogram#accordion1-collapse9)
[**Hotspot Program Summary**](https://dataportal.mt.gov/t/MSL/views/MSL_HotSpotProgram/HotSpotUsage?%3Aembed_code_version=3&%3Aembed=y&%3AloadOrderID=0&%3Adisplay_spinner=no&%3AshowAppBanner=false&%3Adisplay_count=n&%3AshowVizHome=n&%3Aorigin=viz_share_link)
### Funding Sources
The initial setup of the Montana State Library hot spot lending program was funded by the following organizations from 2020-2023:
Institute of Museum and Library Services (LSTA and ARPA funds)  
CARES Act Funds  
Governor's Emergency Education Relief Fund (GEER)  
Steele-Reese Foundation  
Blue Cross and Blue Shield of Montana  
The Trust for Montana Libraries
Funding FY 2024-2025  
Montana Legislature 2023 one-time-only funding: House Bill 2
Starting in Fiscal Year 2026 the funding and management of the hotspot program will be moved to the local level for libraries who would like to/be able to continue the program on their own.
**Thank you to our funders for making this project a possibility!**

# MSL Certification Program
The Montana State Library Commission adopted new rules related to the certification program on December 10, 2025. 
### 10.102.1160 Personnel
(6) The director is or will be certified by the Montana State Library within the required timeframe mandated by the certification program adopted by the Montana State Library Commission.
(a) The purpose of the certification program is to ensure library directors have the foundational skills necessary to manage a public library that meets standards set forth in ARM Subchapter 10.102.11 Public Library Development.
(b) A course of study will be reviewed by the Commission annually for approval at its final meeting of the state fiscal year.
(c) Continuing education credits issued through the State Library certification program are the only eligible credits that can be applied to certification.
(d) The certification program will be reviewed on a regular schedule with no more than 10 years between reviews.
_Effective Date of New Rules: July 1, 2026._
### 2026 Policy Development
The Commission's next step is to adopt updated policies to implement the new rules.
  * [](https://ftpaspen.msl.mt.gov/EventResources/20260105091029_31410.pdf)See the [May 6, 2026 Meeting Event](https://mslservices.mt.gov/ASPeN/Events/Event_Detail.aspx?Event_ID=31769)[](https://forms.office.com/g/4UhiV9jjGu)


* * *
## 2023 Certification Program
#####  Library Director Certification 
##### Initial Certification
60 continuing education credits earned in a 4-year period
  * Library Administration Category: 30 credits
  * Electives: 30 credits in any category


##### Renewal after Initial Certification
  * 60 elective continuing education credits earned in a 4-year period


#####  Trustee Certification 
##### Optional
15 continuing education credits earned in a 4-year period
  * Library Administration Category: 10 credits
  * Electives: 5 credits in any category


#####  Staff Certification 
##### Optional
60 continuing education credits earned in a 4-year period
  * Library Administration Category: 5 credits
  * Library Services to the Public: 5 credits
  * Collection Management and Technical Services: 5 credits
  * Technology: 5 credits
  * Electives: 40 credits in any category


##### [ Certification and Continuing Education Handbook (2023)  ](https://msl.mt.gov/_docs/2023CECERTHandbookFinal.pdf)
##### [ Track Continuing Education Credits in ASPeN  ](https://mslservices.mt.gov/ASPeN/)

# Privacy
### Library Confidentiality
  * [MSL Statement of Privacy and Confidentiality](http://docs.msl.mt.gov/Central_Services/Staff_Handbook/comm_pols/39_privacystmt.pdf)
  * [Library Records Confidentiality Act](http://leg.mt.gov/bills/mca/title_0220/chapter_0010/part_0110/sections_index.html)


### Montana State Library (MSL) Web Site Partners
  * _Third Party Websites_ - MSL often links to our partners' websites with specific privacy policies related to that site. Please be aware of the site you are currently visiting to determine which policy is relevant. You can often find the privacy policy for a website at the bottom of pages. Listed below are the privacy policies for our major partners: 
    * [Archive.org](https://archive.org/about/terms.php)
    * [ASCE](http://www.asce.org/privacy/)
    * [Docline/NIH](http://www.nlm.nih.gov/privacy.html)
    * [Ebsco](https://www.ebsco.com/company/privacy-policy)
    * [ESRI Security and Privacy](http://doc.arcgis.com/en/trust/)
    * [Facebook](https://www.facebook.com/policy.php)
    * [OCLC](https://www.oclc.org/en/policies/privacy.html)
    * [OverDrive](http://company.overdrive.com/privacy-policy/)
    * [Reference USA](http://resource.referenceusa.com/privacy-policy/)
    * [Safari Books](http://www.safaribooksonline.com/privacy/)
    * [Sirsi/Dynix](http://www.sirsidynix.com/privacy)
    * [SlideShare](https://www.linkedin.com/legal/privacy-policy)
    * [Taylor and Francis](http://tandfonline.com/privacy-policy)
    * [Twitter](https://twitter.com/privacy?lang=en)
    * [Vimeo](https://vimeo.com/privacy)  

  * _Google Analytics_ - MSL uses Google Analytics to gather usage reports and trends for our web resources. Please see the links below for more information: 
    * [How Google uses data when you use partner sites or apps](https://www.google.com/policies/privacy/partners/)
    * [Google Analytics Terms of Service](https://www.google.com/analytics/terms/us.html)
    * [Google Privacy Policy](https://www.google.com/policies/privacy/)
    * [How Google uses cookies](https://www.google.com/policies/technologies/cookies/)


### Additional State of Montana Policies Pertaining to Internet Privacy
  * [State of Montana Operations Manual: Internet Privacy & Security Policy](http://mt.gov/1240-X06.pdf)
  * [Montana Code Annotated 2-17-505: Information Technology -- Internet Privacy Policy](http://leg.mt.gov/bills/mca/title_0020/chapter_0170/part_0050/section_0050/0020-0170-0050-0050.html)

# Publishing Rights
![Hands holding book with MSL logo and text that says "Please properly cite the Montana State Library."](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/CiteMSL.png)
Content found through this website, and related applications, that is produced by the Montana State Library is in the public domain. Please properly cite the State Library as the source in any publication. Be aware that some content, such as content in the Montana History Portal, and the GIS Data List, is published by other institutions. Please refer to the publishing institution for permission to publish. Please contact the Montana State Library for more information or for explicit permission to publish specific items or collections.
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)

1201 11th Ave

8AM-5PM


  * Phone: (406) 444-3115   
Toll Free: (800) 338-5087

### Montana Local Governments Web Archive
[Montana Local Governments Web Archive](https://www.archive-it.org/collections/11989 "Montana Local Governments Web Archive") is a web archive of local government websites from Montana counties, cities, towns, public school districts, public libraries, and tribal governments. These local government entities all have a close working relationship with Montana state government. 
To search the web archive, enter your search terms in the box below.
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)

# Applicant Information
Only Montana state employees, state agency contractors, and staff and board members of Montana libraries may obtain library cards from the Montana State Library. Please see the [Circulation & Information Access Policy](http://docs.msl.mt.gov/central_services/staff_handbook/comm_pols/31_circ.pdf) for more details.
* Denotes required field
### Montana State Library
P.O. Box 201800  
1201 11th Avenue  
Helena MT 59620-1800  
406-444-3115  
mslreference@mt.gov  
Hours: 8 am - 5 pm, Monday - Friday

# ILL Policy
Interlibrary loan (ILL) service allows a user of one library to borrow library materials from another library. The Montana State Library (MSL) adheres to the principles endorsed in the [ALA Interlibrary Loan Code](http://www.ala.org/Template.cfm?Section=InterLibrary_Loan&template=/ContentManagement/ContentDisplay.cfm&ContentID=31579), [U.S. Copyright Law](http://www.copyright.gov/title17/), the [CONTU guidelines](http://www.copyright.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/03/White_Paper_ILL-Brochure.pdf) on journal articles, and state laws governing confidentiality of records.
If you have any questions, please email MSLLoan@mt.gov or call 406-444-5352.
[ Who can request ILL materials? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/interlibrary_loan_policy#accordion1-collapse1)
State employees or state agency contractors with a [Montana State Library card](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/state_employee_library_card) may submit ILL requests for work-related materials. Other patrons may request ILL services through their [local public library](http://msl.mt.gov/Library_Development/Library_Directory/default.asp). 
[ How do I request an ILL? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/interlibrary_loan_policy#accordion1-collapse2)
  * [Click here](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/borrowing_request/article_request) to submit an article request
  * [Click here](http://montanastatelib.worldcat.org/) to submit a book request
  * [Click here](http://docline.gov/loansome/login.cfm) to request medical articles using PubMed (tutorial [here](http://docs.msl.mt.gov/lis/pdfs/Ordering%20Loansome%20Doc%20Articles.pdf))
  * Email a request (please include as much information as possible)


[ What is the turnaround time for an ILL? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/interlibrary_loan_policy#accordion1-collapse3)
MSL attempts to process all ILL requests within one business day. Rush requests are accommodated as resources allow. Due to shipping uncertainties, please allow two to three weeks to obtain physical materials. 
[ Are there any charges? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/interlibrary_loan_policy#accordion1-collapse4)
Most ILL items are available free of charge. However, if charged by a lending library, MSL will pay a maximum of $20 for any ILL request. If an ILL item is lost or damaged, the patron will be responsible for any bills charged by the lending library. 
[ What types of materials can be requested? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/interlibrary_loan_policy#accordion1-collapse5)
Books, journal articles, maps, theses, and dissertations can all be requested. However, the below items cannot be obtained through ILL:
  * Books published within the last year
  * Materials not related to the performance of state agency work
  * Materials limited by license agreements
  * Ebooks and eaudiobooks
  * Entire journals/magazines
  * Equipment, hardware, and software


[ Other information ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/interlibrary_loan_policy#accordion1-collapse6)
  * There is no limit to the number of ILL requests.* (Within the guidelines referenced above.)
  * Availability of ILL depends on other libraries and is not guaranteed.
  * The lending library sets the loan period and any restrictions on materials.
  * Materials will be mailed unless otherwise specified.
  * Renewal requests may be made by phone or email.
  * Materials must be returned to MSL by the due date.
  * Lost, late, or damaged materials jeopardize MSL's borrowing privileges.

# Article Request
Interlibrary Loan (ILL) service is available to [s](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/state_employee_library_card)tate employees and contractors. Please view our ILL policy [here](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/interlibrary_loan_policy).
* Denotes required field
**NOTE:** The material you receive through our Interlibrary Loan service may be protected by copyright law.
**The copyright law of the United States (Title 17, U.S. Code) governs the making of photocopies or other reproductions of copyrighted material. Under certain conditions specified in the law, libraries and archives are authorized to furnish a photocopy or other reproduction. One of these specified conditions is that the photocopy or other reproduction is not to be "used for any other purpose other than private study, scholarship, or research." If a user makes a request for, or later uses, a photocopy or reproduction for purposes in excess of “fair use,” that user may be liable for copyright infringement. This institution reserves the right to refuse any copying which, in its judgment, violates copyright law.**

# Notify the Web Archiving Program
Notify us about state webpages needing to be archived or removed.   
* Denotes required fields.
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)

  * **PO Box 201800, or  
1201 11th Ave   
Helena, Montana 59620 **
  * Hours: Monday-Friday   
8AM-5PM

### MT.Gov Web Archive FAQ
[ What is MT.Gov Web Archive? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse1)
MT.Gov Web Archive is an collection of Montana state agency websites dating from 1996. 
[ Why MT.Gov Web Archive?  ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse2)
The Montana State Library uses the MT.Gov Web Archive per [M.C.A. 22-1-212](http://leg.mt.gov/bills/mca/title_0220/chapter_0010/part_0020/section_0120/0220-0010-0020-0120.html) to identify, acquire, catalog, preserve, and provide access to state publications. State agency websites are regarded as state publications per [M.C.A. 22-1-211 (3) (a)](http://leg.mt.gov/bills/mca/title_0220/chapter_0010/part_0020/section_0110/0220-0010-0020-0110.html). It is assumed that state agencies posting information to the World Wide Web intend for that information to be publicly distributed and understand that it may be downloaded, printed out, and cached by machines and users anywhere. The Montana State Library manages this web archive in partial fulfillment of its [statutory mandate](http://leg.mt.gov/bills/mca/title_0220/chapter_0010/part_0020/section_0190/0220-0010-0020-0190.html) to coordinate with state agencies and depository libraries to ensure permanent permanent public access to state publications which in most cases today means the content appearing on state agency websites. The web archive collection is a companion to the text archive collection of [digitized state publications](http://archive.org/details/MontanaStateLibrary/v2).
[ How and when does the MT.Gov Web Archive capture and preserve state agency web sites? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse3)
Montana State Library staff has developed a list of “seeds” or URLs that serve as starting points for scheduled automated crawls of state agency websites. Library staff uses [Archive-It](http://www.archive-it.org/), a web archiving service of the [Internet Archive](http://archive.org/) based in San Francisco, California to capture state agency websites. 
[ How can I search for information in the MT.Gov web archive? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse4)
You can search either by entering a keyword or a state agency URL or web address. Important search tip: browsing the archived state agency website is often faster than sifting through numerous keyword search results. 
[ How can I tell when a web page was archived? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse5)
Archived web pages and their URL display a yellow banner that includes the date archived. Note that PDFs and other files do not display as web pages and thus they do not display a yellow banner indicating that they are archived. Sometimes a web archive link will take you to the live web, if it is linked to a page outside the archive.
[ Does the MT.Gov web archive have limitations? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse6)
The following content is challenging or impossible to archive: web-enabled databases requiring user input, information written in JavaScript, streaming audio, streaming video, navigation menus, and dynamic forms. Search boxes within archived web pages will not function.
[ Why do many state agencies have two domains archived? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse7)
The state government web has used two domain names --- [state.mt.us](http://wayback.archive-it.org/499/query?type=urlquery&url=http%3A%2F%2Fstate.mt.us&date=&Submit=Take+Me+Back) and [mt.gov](http://wayback.archive-it.org/499/query?type=urlquery&url=http%3A%2F%2Fmt.gov&date=&Submit=Take+Me+Back) Sometimes these domains have overlapped each other. A third domain named [discoveringmontana.com](http://wayback.archive-it.org/499/query?type=urlquery&url=http%3A%2F%2Fdiscoveringmontana.com&date=&Submit=Take+Me+Back) appears to duplicate the other two domains. Researchers should check all three domains.
[ Do MT.Gov Web Archive crawlers negatively affecting my agency web server performance?  ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse8)
The archive.org_bot does not consume much bandwith. No state agency web manager has reported bandwith issues from the archive.org_bot
[ What Montana state agency domains does MT.Gov Web Archive crawl? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse9)
Our web crawler crawls just external, not internal domains. MT.Gov Web Archive **__does not__** crawl test or development web servers.
[ How do I notify the MT.Gov Web Archive staff about missing web pages or a state website about to be removed? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse10)
Use this [notification form.](https://msl.mt.gov/research/interlibrary_loan/borrowing_request/Notify_the_Web_Archiving_Program)
[ What if I have concerns about content appearing in the MT.Gov Web Archive? ](https://msl.mt.gov/research/state_publications/mtgov_connect/mtgov_connect_faq#accordion1-collapse11)
Content found within MT.Gov Web Archive is part of the [MSL Commission Collection Development Policy.](https://msl.mt.gov/_docs/Collection-Development-Policy.pdf) Submit any concerns on page 8 of the [MSL Commission Collection Development Policy](https://msl.mt.gov/_docs/Collection-Development-Policy.pdf).

# Embed "Page History"
Note: "Page History" or "Page Archive" is already part of the State of Montana web template. If your state agency does not use the state web template and wants to provide immediate public access to former versions of individual pages on your agency website, copy and paste the code below into your state agency website footer.
`<a href="javascript:location.href='https://wayback.archive-it.org/499/*/'+document.location.href;" title="Get Webpage History">Page History</a>`
![MSL Logo](https://msl.mt.gov/_images/MSL-GSLong_grayRev.png)

## Use of Google Analytics
**The Montana State Library website uses cookies.**
We want to make our website more user-friendly and continuously improve it. We use cookies to collect anonymous information. For example, cookies collect information on what pages were visited and how long each visitor stayed on a page. This anonymous information is used to improve our website content, design, and the services we offer. If you continue to use our website, you agree to the use of cookies.
This website specifically uses Google Analytics to analyze web traffic. Google uses cookies to collect anonymous web traffic data, which the State Library uses to improve our online services, information and user experience. Through our use of the Google Analytics application, neither the State Library nor Google collect personally identifiable information.
The following information may be automatically collected and retained when you view or search through MDA websites, or download information:
  * The type of browser and operating system used to visit the site;
  * The date and time of when you access the site; and
  * Which portions of the website you visit.


We do not attempt to gain personally identifiable information about individual users and associate it with IP addresses. The State does not use the information collected to ascertain your personally identifiable information.
To learn more about cookies, Google Analytics, and internet privacy policies and laws in Montana, please refer to:
  * [How Google Uses Cookies](https://policies.google.com/technologies/cookies)
  * [How Google Uses Information from Sites that Use Google Services](https://policies.google.com/technologies/partner-sites)
  * [Google Privacy Policy](https://policies.google.com/privacy)
  * [Google Analytics Opt-out Add-on](https://tools.google.com/dlpage/gaoptout?hl=en)
  * [How Google Uses Data When You Use Partner Sites or Apps](https://www.google.com/policies/privacy/partners/)
  * [Google Analytics Terms of Service](https://www.google.com/analytics/terms/us.html)
  * [State of Montana Operations Manual: Internet Privacy & Security Policy](http://mt.gov/1240-X06.pdf)
  * [Montana Code Annotated 2-17-505: Information Technology -- Internet Privacy Policy](http://leg.mt.gov/bills/mca/title_0020/chapter_0170/part_0050/section_0050/0020-0170-0050-0050.html)
